##### ↳ ↳ Re: opening indexed file from within a class

- **From:** "Charles Hottel" <chottel@cpcug.org>
- **Date:** 2002-10-13T20:39:33+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<01c272f8$97617e40$62c2f943@chottel>`
- **References:** `<3da8d535@dnews.tpgi.com.au> <3da94a4f_3@Usenet.com>`

```
Here is Proj0401 r05-drvr.cbl :

       $set sourceformat "free"
*>************************************************
*> Room Rental System
*> W. Price  Nov 23, 1999            R05-DRVR.CBL
*>
*> This driver provides the user a menu allowing 
*> for full room prices, discounted room prices, 
*> or room capacity.  It illustrates invoking 
*> different methods of the room class.
*> The following classes comprise this project:
*>   r05-room   Room
*>************************************************

Identification Division.
       Program-ID.  Room05Driver.

Environment Division.
       Object Section.
         Class-control.
          RoomClass is class "r05-room"
         .
Data Division.
  Working-Storage Section.

    01  room-prices.
        10  std-config-price      pic 9(03).
        10  spec-config-price     pic 9(03).
    01  room-capacity             pic 9(02).

    01  menu-choice               pic X(01).
        88  discounted-prices       value "D" "d".
        88  standard-prices         value "S" "s".

    01  theRoomHandle   usage object reference.

Procedure Division.
  000-process-room-data.

    *> Create an instance of the room object
    Invoke RoomClass "new"
                     Returning theRoomHandle
    Perform 850-get-menu-selection
    Evaluate TRUE
      When discounted-prices
        Invoke theRoomHandle
                    "get-discounted-room-prices"
                    Returning room-prices
        Perform 900-display-room-prices
      When standard-prices
        Invoke theRoomHandle "get-room-prices"
                    Returning room-prices
        Perform 900-display-room-prices
      When other
        Invoke theRoomHandle "get-room-capacity"
                    Returning room-capacity
        Perform 950-display-room-capacity
    End-evaluate *>TRUE
    Stop run
    .
  850-get-menu-selection.
    Display " "
    Display "The options are:"
    Display "  C - Room capacity (default)"
    Display "  S - Standard room prices"
    Display "  D - Discounted room prices"
    Display "   "
    Display "Your choice <C,S,D>? " no advancing
    Accept menu-choice
    .
  900-display-room-prices.
    Display " "
    Display "Standard configuration price: " 
                               std-config-price 
    Display "Special configuration price:   " 
                              spec-config-price 
    .
  950-display-room-capacity.
    Display " "
    Display "Room capacity: " room-capacity
    .

<3da94a4f_3@Usenet.com>...

##### ↳ ↳ Re: opening indexed file from within a class

- **From:** "Charles Hottel" <chottel@cpcug.org>
- **Date:** 2002-10-13T20:40:31+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<01c272f8$baa31120$62c2f943@chottel>`
- **References:** `<3da8d535@dnews.tpgi.com.au> <3da94a4f_3@Usenet.com>`

```
Here is Proj040` r05-room.cbl  :
       $set sourceformat "free"
*>*************************************************
*> Room Rental System
*> W. Price  Nov 23, 1999             R05-ROOM.CBL
*>
*> This class is similar to R04-ROOM except it 
*> utilizes the OBJECT paragraph for the room
*> object rather than the FACTORY paragraph.
*> Thus it is necessary to create an instance of
*> the room object.
*> Methods.
*>   get-discounted-room-prices
*>   get-room-capacity
*>   get-room-prices
*>*************************************************

Identification Division.
       Class-id.  RoomClass 
                  inherits from BaseClass
                  .
Environment Division.
       Object Section.
         Class-control.
          RoomClass is class "r05-room"
          BaseClass is class "base"
         .
*>=================================================

OBJECT.
  Data Division.
    Object-Storage Section.
    01  room-data.
        10  room-number     pic X(03)  value "100".
        10  std-config-price  pic 9(03)  value 225.
        10  spec-config-price pic 9(03)  value 385.
        10  room-discount     pic v9(02) value .05.
        10  room-capacity     pic 9(02)  value 38.

  Procedure Division.

    *>---------------------------------------------
    Method-id. get-discounted-room-prices.
    *>---------------------------------------------
      Data Division.
        Local-Storage Section.
          01  lo-price-factor         pic 9(01)v9(02).

        Linkage Section.
          01  ls-room-prices.
              10  ls-std-config-price   pic 9(03).
              10  ls-spec-config-price  pic 9(03).

      Procedure Division Returning ls-room-prices.
        Move std-config-price to ls-std-config-price
        Move spec-config-price to ls-spec-config-price
        Subtract room-discount from 1.0
                                 giving lo-price-factor
        Multiply lo-price-factor 
                             by ls-std-config-price
        Multiply lo-price-factor 
                             by ls-spec-config-price
          .
    End Method get-discounted-room-prices.

    *>---------------------------------------------
    Method-id. get-room-prices.
    *>---------------------------------------------
      Data Division.
        Linkage Section.
          01  ls-room-prices.
              10  ls-std-config-price    pic 9(03).
              10  ls-spec-config-price   pic 9(03).

      Procedure Division  Returning ls-room-prices.
        Move std-config-price to ls-std-config-price
        Move spec-config-price to ls-spec-config-price
        .
    End Method get-room-prices.

    *>-----------------------------------------------
    Method-id. get-room-capacity.
    *>-----------------------------------------------
      Data Division.
        Linkage Section.
          01  ls-room-capacity             pic 9(02).

      Procedure Division  Returning ls-room-capacity.
        Move room-capacity to ls-room-capacity
        .
    End Method get-room-capacity.
    *>-----------------------------------------------
END OBJECT.
END CLASS RoomClass.

## Thread: COBOL FAQ — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Meta: FAQs, group policy, charter`](topics.md#meta)_

### COBOL FAQ

- **From:** wmklein@ix.netcom.com (William M. Klein)
- **Date:** 2002-10-13T15:34:00+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol,news.answers,comp.answers
- **Message-ID:** `<computer-lang/cobol-faq_1034523049@rtfm.mit.edu>`

```
Archive-name: computer-lang/cobol-faq
Posting-Frequency: twice a month
Last-Modified: 2002/05/06
Version: 3.03
URL: http://www.cobolreport.com/faqs/cobolfaq.htm
Reply-To: wmklein@ix.netcom.com


                            COBOL FAQ
                  (Frequently Asked Questions)

Last-Modified: Spring 2002

The full COBOL FAQ can be viewed at:

  http://www.cobolreport.com/faqs/cobolfaq.htm

If you have comments, corrects, deletions, or additions, please send
private email to:

    wmklein <at> ix.netcom.com

Toward the top of the FAQ is a pointer to the appendix listing the most
recent significant updates and changes.

This FAQ answers such questions as (and addresses topics such as):

 - Where can I get a COBOL compiler? 
 - Is there a free COBOL compiler? 
 - Where can I contact... ?
 - What is happening with the draft of the next COBOL Standard and what
is in it? 
 - What about OO COBOL? 
 - Books about COBOL
 - COBOL Tools
 - What can/should I post in the COBOL newsgroups?
 - What about USAGE? COMP? Storage for data in xyz format? etc?
 - How do I get started with COBOL? Where can I get education?
Tutorials? Etc

and much, MUCH more
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Power Cobol

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2002-10-15T10:50:14+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<GpSq9.3393$qW4.1409413@newssrv26.news.prodigy.com>`
- **References:** `<1926936.1034609867@dbforums.com> <3DAB10C8.4030806@sympatico.ca> <3dab4f41_7@Usenet.com> <3DAB6D7F.8040508@sympatico.ca>`

```
"Donald Tees" <Donald_Tees@sympatico.ca> wrote in message
news:3DAB6D7F.8040508@sympatico.ca...
> Corrected by both now.  I thought they did bring one in with the newer
> versions, but now that I think about it, the reason I never upgraded was
>   the restriction about me only being able to use one machine. That
> makes developing stuff on my network as annoying as hell.

The policy of 'one license=one user only' makes sense for end-user software,
but not for software which itself is used to develop other software.

My favorite - and one about which I have written the publisher (on real
paper!) - is the Mercator Software mapping product.

Mercator is a very fine product, but at $10K up front and $2K/year
maintenance for a PC product, it is beyond comprehension that (if you follow
the letter of the license) you may not have a development machine and a
production machine simultaneously running the software, even if the
'production' machine uses only the run-time support module to execute the
maps you compile on the development machine.

I am an unabashed fan of the Mercator product, but trying to develop new or
modified Mercator components USING THE PRODUCTION SYSTEM is about the
dumbest thing one could possibly do, what with PC prices what they are; not
to mention the term 'production machine' suggests a Real User might actually
be using the equipment and software during business hours.

Seems to me any publisher marketing development software utilizing a
runtime - which includes many COBOL and other language compilers - would be
well-advised to adopt an 'out of the box' policy of one development license
= one license for the development part of the product plus two runtimes: one
for the developer and one for a non-developer (production) user. Second
license for a second developer? No problem.  Extra 'run-time only' licenses
for additional 'run-time only' users? No problem.

I've often expressed concern that developers of compilers and other tools
live in Fantasyland, and really do not have a clue what we applications
developers - their customers - face out here in The Real World. These
tunnel-vision marketing policies do nothing to disabuse me of that notion.
```

> I am an unabashed fan of the Mercator product, but trying to develop new or

then this doesn't apply.

testing multiple access to the system for such things as locking.

Certainly the publisher could add in a production run-time system in
the compiler bundle, but they would just put the price up to cover it.

> I've often expressed concern that developers of compilers and other tools

OTOH they probably think that their customers live in fantasy land
wanting it  for free.
Of course I want all my software for free too.

Michael, I have a lot of sympathy for what you are saying here. I've had

I honestly believe that there is no clear pricing policy because times are
so tough it is a case of "charge whatever the traffic will bear" for some
vendors.

If they give you a price and you accept it, then they find out you are
really a corporation (or even a small business) they groan because they
believe (rightly or wrongly...) that they could've extracted more... On the
other hand if they give you a price which is too high they will lose your
business. Have you tried making an offer? Like, "I don't want to pay more
than X". If the response is "Sorry..." then you can legitimately ask what
the price is. (They must know because your offer was unacceptable...).

Another alternative is to play the e-bay card. I have done this a couple of
times and achieved a good discount. "Well, I guess I could a get a copy from
e-bay, but I'd rather have it first hand...Is that really the very best you
can do?"

If they are struggling to make the sales quota (and many are at the moment)
they tend to be agreeable.

I agree that it is irritating on the extreme when there is no standard
pricing policy. It is a bit like airline seats; the guys sitting next to you
did not pay the same price you did, or even the same price as each other
<G>.

Will be interested to see how  you get on with Mercator.

Pete.



 Posted Via Usenet.com Premium Usenet Newsgroup Services
----------------------------------------------------------
    ** SPEED ** RETENTION ** COMPLETION ** ANONYMITY **
----------------------------------------------------------        
                http://www.usenet.com
```

_(thread depth: 8)_

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2002-10-17T10:40:04+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8swr9.3804$qW4.1711370@newssrv26.news.prodigy.com>`
- **References:** `<1926936.1034609867@dbforums.com> <3DAB10C8.4030806@sympatico.ca> <3dab4f41_7@Usenet.com> <3DAB6D7F.8040508@sympatico.ca> <GpSq9.3393$qW4.1409413@newssrv26.news.prodigy.com> <217e491a.0210151347.2d30627d@posting.google.com> <Fdbr9.3572$qW4.1561540@newssrv26.news.prodigy.com> <3dadf957_4@Usenet.com>`

```
"Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz> wrote in message
news:3dadf957_4@Usenet.com...
>
> Michael Mattias <michael.mattias@gte.net> wrote in message
> news:Fdbr9.3572$qW4.1561540@newssrv26.news.prodigy.com...
>
> [complants about inability to get a price quote from software vendors]

>  Have you tried making an offer? Like, "I don't want to pay more
> than X". If the response is "Sorry..." then you can legitimately ask what
> the price is. (They must know because your offer was unacceptable...).

My purpose was to obtain the "manufacturers suggested retail price," not to
actually make a purchase.

I am often asked to recommend/suggest various pieces of commercial software,
and I feel the price is a legitimate part of my deliberation. I do not
participate in VAR programs or accept finders' fees or commissions - my
recommendations are based solely on my experience with the software and
analysis of a client's needs. Should the client decide to proceed, I give
him a phone number and stay out of his interaction with the vendor. I
explain all this to the vendors and still encounter resistance.....

On the Mercator thing... I did receive the pricing I requested from the
sales rep for Wisconsin in an email yesterday.

Run-time only "bundles" are available for $15,000 for a package of ten, or
$20,000 for a package of twenty. The 'run-time only' packages do not include
any of the I-O adapters other than the 'standard' adapters. (If you are not
familiar with Mercator, the I-O adapters are kind of a specialty thing which
make certain things possible without writing a piece of 'middleware'  or
going through another layer of software. Not necessary, but really, really
handy).

When I questioned if the rep had made a typo, he said no, them was the
numbers. I suggested Mercator was eschewing the entry-level market; he
readily acknowledged that Mercator's focus was, indeed, on the larger firm
(he suggested the $1,000,000,000 sales size, but I think that was
figurative - and maybe his own frustration).  That's too bad, because there
is almost no one in the EDI translation-mapping software business who offers
an economical way for small vertical market developers (i.e., myself) to add
an 'edi-enabled' option to their vertical market products, and asking the
entry-level user to both pay these kinds of numbers and/or learn 'another
system' is a real inhibition.

Fortunately, it is 'most' and not 'all' vendors - there is one firm who has
been receptive to my pleas for something entry-level and designed for
vertical market developers/integrators, and I am very close to making a 'go'
decision on a proposal they put together. (You've got to love vendors who
can actually think beyond the current product/price list and figure out you
make as much money selling 100 copies at $500 each as you do selling one
copy at $50,000 - more, if you consider those 100 little guys' aggregate
potential for their $50,000 product is precisely zero.)

This is obviously one of my hot buttons, and since I think I am beginning
(again) to ramble, I'll stop now.

MCM
```

```
The cost of support is probably greater for 50 small customers with 10
seats each is probably higher than for one customer with 500 seats even
though the support cost per small customer may smaller.  In addition
there is a certain amount of fixed cost per sale such as distribution,
billing, and sales time.  Also the larger customer may not be willing to
pay prices based on size such that they may not be willing to pay 10
times as much for 100 seats as they would for 10 seats.  Pricing is a
zoo for both sides.  Take a look at the complaints about pricing of
small use applications on IBM mainframes in the archives of ibm-main at
bama.ua.edu. 

Michael Mattias wrote:
> 
> "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz> wrote in message

> MCM

```
"Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net> wrote in message news:<GpSq9.3393

> The policy of 'one license=one user only' makes sense for end-user software,
> but not for software which itself is used to develop other software.
> 

I disagree.  It's like a book.  I worked for a software company that
used a hardware key.  They didn't care how many machines you had it
installed on - just so it only ran on one per license at any given
time.  Two people can't use the same book at the same time - without
being in close proximity.  If they both need to read the book at the
same time - you buy a second book.

Fujitsu allows you to purchase additional licenses for the cost of
maintenance.  That's fair.

The license is easy to transfer from machine to machine.
```

If you have the original cd, when you install the product, there is an
option to install the runtime file in a folder called WRAPPER..
Once you have installed it, in this folder there are 4 setup
applications.
You need to add these setup's file with your application cd, then
install them on customer machine.. It's the more easy way.

Hope in this help.

Gianni

## Thread: gdb with IBM-COBOL on aix — 3 msgs

### gdb with IBM-COBOL on aix

- **From:** "Torsten Reichert" <Thorsten.Reichert@dresdner-bank.com>
- **Date:** 2002-10-15T15:49:51+02:00

```
Is there any way to use gdb on COBOL programs generated with IBM's compiler
on aix ?

Thank you very much

P.S.: Just to be sort of complete
1PP 5765-548 IBM COBOL Set for AIX 1.1
$ gdb --version
GNU gdb 5.2.1: This GDB was configured as "powerpc-ibm-aix4.3.3.0".
```

#### ↳ gdb seems unable to display variables

- **From:** "Torsten Reichert" <Thorsten.Reichert@dresdner-bank.com>
- **Date:** 2002-10-15T17:06:27+02:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<aoh9ss$gng2@news-1.bank.dresdner.net>`
- **References:** `<aoh5d8$gn62@news-1.bank.dresdner.net>`

```
After starting a program, attaching gdb and stepping through, it does not
display variables:
gdb) p KONSTANTEN
$2 = {PGM-NAME = <optimized out or zero length>, CVS-TEXT = <incomplete
type>}

That they are not optimized away, is suggested by the following observations
1) xldb displays all variables
2) cob2 does not even have optimization options

I suppose the problem comes from the dash signs taht are valid in COBOL
names, that gdb interprets as minus signs.
Another possibillity would be that gdb does not know the storage layout of
IBM's compiler.

Has anyone found the solution already ?

Thank you
```

### COBOL in the .NET and WSED 5.0

- **From:** Gareth.Kruse@gmx.net (Gareth)

```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL in the .NET and WSED 5.0

- **From:** "JerryMouse" <nospam@bisusa.com>
- **Date:** 2002-10-16T08:17:04-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bAudnadBrdBS-zCgXTWcqA@News.GigaNews.Com>`

- **From:** "Acucorp" <shaun_gough@hotmail.com>
- **Date:** 2002-10-18T11:31:54-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<DA91646D29C2DF4A85EC32EA1C484BEB1FEE29@ras.acucorp.com>`
- **References:** `<1935297.1034780930@dbforums.com> <DA91646D29C2DF4A85EC32EA1C484BEB1FC04D@ras.acucorp.com> <1945071.1034956867@dbforums.com>`

```
Hi.

Please check that the ODBC product that you are using does not require a
username and password to open a connection, if this is needed then, you can
use the A-ODBC-LOGIN and A-ODBC-PASSWD to do specify this.   If this does
not work then, check the XFD file that you have created, and check that the
name of the table is correct for the connection phase, if this is not the
same, then you can specify the name within the XFD file, by using the XFD
NAME directive within the FD source.

If you continue to have problems, please do not hesitate to contact me.
```

<a id="t-25e4d7860f"></a>
## Thread: AcuCobol 4GL — 2 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers)_

### AcuCobol 4GL

- **From:** "Augie Murphy" <augieMurphy@sbcglobal.net>
- **Date:** 2002-10-18T04:54:41+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<luMr9.5676$ML3.360903003@newssvr21.news.prodigy.com>`

```
Is it possible to have one AcuCobol 4GL application access 2 databases on 2
different computers. One database on the same server as the application and
one on a database server? Both are Oracle.
```

#### ↳ Re: AcuCobol 4GL

- **From:** "Acucorp" <shaun_gough@hotmail.com>
- **Date:** 2002-10-18T12:32:56-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<DA91646D29C2DF4A85EC32EA1C484BEB1FF09D@ras.acucorp.com>`
- **References:** `<luMr9.5676$ML3.360903003@newssvr21.news.prodigy.com>`

```
Dear Augie.

It is possible to connect to two different Oracle databases being hosted on
different server machine.   All that needs to be done within the COBOL code,
is to ensure that the ORACLE_HOME, ORACLE_SID and LD_LIBRARY_PATH are set up
correctly prior to the opening of the file, and the Runtime will connect to
the correct Database on the correct Server machine.

Please do not hesitate to contact your local Acucorp office if you need any
further assistance in doing this.
```

#### ↳ Re: Printing problems

- **From:** Donald Tees <Donald_Tees@Sympatico.ca>

poopiehead wrote:

> I have a few problems actually.
>
…[19 more quoted lines elided]…

On the later one, it is pretty obvious that index-num never becomes greater
than table-num.  What is the value of table-num, and what is the picture
clause of index-num.  Changing the "print-table (index-num)" to a simple
"index-num" should put the value on the print line.  If it does not climb to
the right value and stop, you will see what the error is.  Probably too
small a picture clause ... like expecting picture 99 to become greater than
99.

Donald
```

#### ↳ Re: Printing problems

- **From:** riplin@Azonic.co.nz (Richard)
- **Date:** 2002-10-22T00:05:58-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<217e491a.0210212305.5ee16b11@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<1954564.1035225954@dbforums.com>`

```
poopiehead <member@dbforums.com> wrote 

> I have a few problems actually.

Let us guess: you are actually using Fujitsu 3 on Windows 98, but you
didn't think that it was worth mentioning because "all computers are
Windows, aren't they ?, and all Cobols are exactly the same.".
 
> First I am trying to print to a printer.  I have to select the printer
> with the key word printer.  I can't open with select blah-blah assign to
> "LPT1".  I have to select blah-blah assign to printer.  Since this is
> always mapped to my default printer is there a way to change my default
> printer WITH OUT using a print dialog box.  
I want the application
> automatic and I don't want it to be user specied.

The Fujitsu 3 'User's Guide' specifies that the SELECT ASSIGN for a
printer may be to:

             PRINTER
             "LPTn:"         (note colon, eg "LPT1:")
             "COMn:"

Note that using LPT1: may require that the printer be setup in Windows
with 'capture' for this port.

Manuals can be useful sometimes.  In fact it has a whole chapter (8)
on printing.

> Second I am writing a program and I can't seem to get the program to
> print properly.  It either spits out a thousands copies (endless loop I
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> end-perform.

You don't specifiy whether it only prints the first item in the table,
or whether it prints all the items in the table but all on one line
that is hundreds of characters long (and therefore falls off the edge
of the page).

Try using a write statement that is suitable for a printer, such as:

        write print-record BEFORE ADVANCING 1 LINE

This is also covered in Chapter 8 of the manual.

Manuals are available for download from www.adtools.com.

> I want the application
> automatic and I don't want it to be user specied.

Note that if it is Fujitsu version 3 and it is a downloaded version
then the licence that you agreed to prohibits you from distributing
applications to users.  If you obtained it in some other way then you
need to read the licence for that version.
```

#### ↳ Re: Printing problems

- **From:** poopiehead <member@dbforums.com>
- **Date:** 2002-10-22T11:55:07+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1957240.1035287707@dbforums.com>`

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Printing problems

- **From:** Frederico Fonseca <frederico_fonseca@eudoramail.com>

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Printing problems

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2002-10-23T07:06:17+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3DB63C59.F6F6779D@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<1954564.1035225954@dbforums.com> <1957240.1035287707@dbforums.com>`

```
poopiehead wrote:
> 
> I am running fujitsu cobol v6.1 on a windows 98 machine.  

> Printer is defined as follows
>        SELECT PRINT-FILE
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>                SELECT PRINT-FILE ASSIGN TO PRINTER-PORT

Printers need a CR (Carriage Return - resets position to start of
current line) and LF (Line Feed - feeds paper to next line) on the end
of each print line.  This can be given by write .. BEFORE ADVANCING 1
LINE (or AFTER if you prefer) or it can be specified as being
automatically added by SELECT ... ORGANIZATION LINE SEQUENTIAL (rather
that the default of SEQUENTIAL).

Without these there is a possibility that all the print data will appear
on one line hundreds of characters long, well past the edge of the
paper.

This is covered in the manual.

Now what was the actual problem you were having ?
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Printing problems

- **From:** rob lee <nospam@rr.com>
- **Date:** 2002-10-23T12:18:20+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3DB69256.FD483EB7@rr.com>`
- **References:** `<1954564.1035225954@dbforums.com> <1957240.1035287707@dbforums.com>`

```


poopiehead wrote:
> 
> I am running fujitsu cobol v6.1 on a windows 98 machine. 
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> 

My limited experience with printing from Fujitsu involves assigning the
printer to a name like PRINTER-1, then mapping that name to a network
printer in the COBOL85.CBR environment file using their configuration
utility.  The utility is somewhat awkward but is the best way to end up
with valid values in the CBR file.

This was the simplest method of addressing a system printer detailed in
the Fuji docs.
```

                            COBOL FAQ
                  (Frequently Asked Questions)

  http://www.cobolreport.com/faqs/cobolfaq.htm

If you have comments, corrects, deletions, or additions, please send

    wmklein <at> ix.netcom.com

Toward the top of the FAQ is a pointer to the appendix listing the most
recent significant updates and changes.

This FAQ answers such questions as (and addresses topics such as):

 - Where can I get a COBOL compiler? 
 - Is there a free COBOL compiler? 
 - Where can I contact... ?
 - What is happening with the draft of the next COBOL Standard and what
is in it? 
 - What about OO COBOL? 
 - Books about COBOL
 - COBOL Tools
 - What can/should I post in the COBOL newsgroups?
 - What about USAGE? COMP? Storage for data in xyz format? etc?
 - How do I get started with COBOL? Where can I get education?
Tutorials? Etc

and much, MUCH more

<a id="t-d0e953946b"></a>
## Thread: Group Focused on SQL/XML Specifications Picks INCITS to Develop Standards — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`COBOL standards (ANS, ISO, 74/85/2002/2014)`](topics.md#standards) · [`Databases and SQL`](topics.md#databases) · [`Web, XML, modern integration`](topics.md#web)_

### Group Focused on SQL/XML Specifications Picks INCITS to Develop Standards

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-10-21T16:38:16-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ap1s4f$rlk$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
Per,
  http://www.incits.org/press/2002/pr200210h2xml.htm

"Group Focused on SQL/XML Specifications Picks INCITS to Develop Standards
Oracle to Host November 6 Meeting; Open to All Interested Parties

Washington, D.C. October 18, 2002 - The SQLX Group, which has been
developing specifications related to the combined use of SQL and XML since
2000, has voted to formalize its work through the InterNational Committee
for Information Technology Standards (INCITS). The new organization, which
will be known as Task Group H2.3, will be part of INCITS Technical Committee
H2-Database.

"While the SQLX Group worked well for two years, members recently became
aware of some disadvantages associated with their informal mode of
operation," explained Kate McMillan, director of the Secretariat for INCITS.
"As a result, representatives from member companies asked INCITS' H2 to
establish a new Task Group so that future proposals linked to the SQL/XML
specification could be developed within the de jure standards environment."
INCITS has worked in the de jure standards arena since 1961, when it was
first accredited by the American National Standards Institute."
```

<a id="t-b12a5ab1fa"></a>
## Thread: TinyCOBOL release version 0.59 — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Open-source COBOL (GnuCOBOL, OpenCOBOL, TinyCOBOL)`](topics.md#open-source)_

### TinyCOBOL release version 0.59

- **From:** "Bernard Giroud" <bernard.giroud@creditlyonnais.ch>
- **Date:** 2002-10-22T18:58:22+02:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3db58431$0$254$626a54ce@news.free.fr>`

```
Hi All,

The TinyCOBOL compiler version 0.59 is available for download at the TC
home page (1) and iBiblio (2).

This release contains mainly bugs fixes, and some enhancements.  It includes
updates to the main compiler and run-time.
Support for internationalization (en, pr_BR, it, fr) has been added.
Improvements have been made in the following areas: multi-linecomment
entries in the identification division, run-time errorreporting, and plenty
of new intrinsics.
Finally, there is now only one library, shared by default.

Please report any bugs and/or problems to the TC mailing list.


Bernard Giroud

1) TinyCOBOL Home Page
   http://tiny-cobol.sourceforge.net/

2) iBiblio (formerly Metalab)
   http://www.ibiblio.org/pub/Linux/devel/lang/cobol/
```

## Thread: Bank of America is UN-AMERICAN — 35 msgs

### Bank of America is UN-AMERICAN

- **From:** "Ken Mullins" <**Ken**Mullins**@**mindspring.com** remove **'s>
- **Date:** 2002-10-22T20:00:01-04:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ap4omp$7mt$1@nntp2-cm.news.eni.net>`

```
http://www.charlotte.com/mld/charlotte/business/industries/banking/4338944.h
tm

More IT (COBOL programming) jobs are being outsourced to India...When will
it end?...Is 3-5 BILLION dollars of pure profit not enough for BOA?

Definitely helping COBOL's demise here in the USA...Banks have been one of
the biggest users of COBOL...


Some text from the article...


Employee unrest

Some of the company's technology employees, many of them programmers with an
average salary of $70,000 to $100,000, say they are waiting to see who will
lose their jobs next.

Laid-off employees said they have been asked to sign two sets of papers: One
states that the employee will receive two weeks' severance for every year he
or she worked for the bank. The other says severance will be canceled if the
employees talk to the media or quit before a certain date. They've also been
asked to help train their Indian counterparts before their final day.

A small group of current and former employees told The Observer last week it
was difficult to work with their futures being uncertain. They worried about
finding work and the prospect of leaving Charlotte in search of high-tech
jobs. A few even talked of leaving the technology world.

"The days of being a developer at Bank of America are numbered," said a
programmer worried about supporting a wife and children.

The employees declined to give their names on the record, for fear of losing
their jobs or severance.

A few were sipping beers, saying that it didn't matter what they did because
their jobs were gone anyway.

"I call it being fired," one programmer said.
```

#### ↳ Re: Bank of America is UN-AMERICAN

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com
- **Date:** 2002-10-22T22:22:29-04:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ap5155$l0e$1@panix1.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<ap4omp$7mt$1@nntp2-cm.news.eni.net>`

```
In article <ap4omp$7mt$1@nntp2-cm.news.eni.net>,
Ken Mullins <**Ken**Mullins**@**mindspring.com** remove **'s> wrote:
>http://www.charlotte.com/mld/charlotte/business/industries/banking/4338944.h

>
>More IT (COBOL programming) jobs are being outsourced to India...When will
>it end?...Is 3-5 BILLION dollars of pure profit not enough for BOA?

In a word... no.  Unless it is legally defined as 'windfall' then I do not 
know of any management training which teaches how to calculate 'This Much 
Profit and Not a Penny More.'

Consider: if folks at the bank know of a way to make more profit and do 
*not* implement it then they are shirking their duties to the 
shareholders.

DD
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Bank of America is UN-AMERICAN

- **From:** dashwood@enternet.co.nz (Peter E. C. Dashwood)
- **Date:** 2002-10-23T04:25:18-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<b3638c46.0210230325.36565052@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<ap4omp$7mt$1@nntp2-cm.news.eni.net> <ap5155$l0e$1@panix1.panix.com>`

```
I was fascinated by Ken's post. It raises a number of issues.

Response to the Doc's response, below.

docdwarf@panix.com wrote in message news:<ap5155$l0e$1@panix1.panix.com>...
> In article <ap4omp$7mt$1@nntp2-cm.news.eni.net>,
> Ken Mullins <**Ken**Mullins**@**mindspring.com** remove **'s> wrote:
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
> DD
 
This seems to be a perfect case of what Don was saying about the
morality of big Business.

If a company makes $3.5 billion profit, do they have any more
obligation to their employees than a company that makes $3000 (or,
indeed, .30c profit...)?

The Doc says their obligation is to do their utmost for the
Shareholders.

(As a shareholder myself in various Companies, I have great sympathy
for this point of view, and it would be a brave person indeed who
would argue against it...<G>)

But should this pursuit of profit be to the exclusion of all else?

Personally, I don't think so...

Has anyone actually ASKED the shareholders of BOA whether they are
comfortable with this action, or is it simply assumed that
maximisation of profit MUST be done?

Some years ago I attended an AGM of the German Company BAYER (they of
aspirin fame...although many people would not realise that Bayer are
into dyes, fertilisers, plastics, all kinds of stuff as well as
pharmaceuticals, and all around the World..), held in Koeln (Cologne),
Germany.

I was amazed to see on the agenda the question of wages for African
workers. It had been raised, as these workers were receiving less than
the minimum guaranteed in Germany. (In fact the workers were well paid
by local standards, and had good conditions, staff canteens etc.) The
Board responded to this question by making the point that the money
being paid was adequate for the local conditions. The response from
the floor was that the company had made significant billions of DM
profit, and therefore had an obligation to its workers. There was some
heated debate and finally it was put to a vote. It was carried, and
the workers were granted the minimum wage payable in Germany (a
princely sum by the local standards.)

I was surprised by this because you wouldn't think that shareholders
would vote against their own interests. Nevertheless, on that
occasion, they did.

(I don't know whether it was actually implemented, but I have no
reason to believe it wasn't.)

If a Company pays somebody $2000 a week to maintain their IT and
another Company (or Country)comes along and says "We'll do it for $30
a week..." it would be foolish to be surprised when a deal is
struck... The immediate solution is a no-brainer. But the implications
of this can be much more far-reaching.

It would be unreasonable (and unfair) to place a jobs embargo on India
(or any other Country or Company which is simply trying to make an
honest living) but it should also be unacceptable to destroy the local
community. This is where, I believe, the size of the profit DOES have
a bearing. To demand unlimited profits, irrespective of the Human
Cost, is just bad economics. What point is there in having all the
money if you cannot enjoy it, because your community has been
destroyed?

I believe that outsourcing is morally and economically inevitable. But
it should be done over an acceptable period of time (say 2 years
minimum and 5 is better), every effort should be made to help staff
who will become redundant, funds should be allocated for retraining
and redeployment. Severance payments should be generous. People who
volunteer for early redundacy should be given an even better package.
All of this can be financed from the large profit.

I would stress that this is not just from motives of generosity; it is
the most effective way to minimise the effect of outsourcing on the
local community.

Shareholders should be apprised that a percentage of profit is being
witheld to ease the pain of redundancy, and to minimise the impact on
the local community.

If we take a long term view, we can see the economies of the 3rd World
being improved, standards of living rising, and eventually they will
price themselves off the market, just as we have. At that point we
should have a level playing field, but by then, it will be irrelevant
as far as "computer programming" is concerned...

Finally, if I were a BOA shareholder I'd be thinking about the
AGM...<G>
Pete.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Bank of America is UN-AMERICAN

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com
- **Date:** 2002-10-23T09:19:32-04:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ap67l4$p4e$1@panix1.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<ap4omp$7mt$1@nntp2-cm.news.eni.net> <ap5155$l0e$1@panix1.panix.com> <b3638c46.0210230325.36565052@posting.google.com>`

```
In article <b3638c46.0210230325.36565052@posting.google.com>,
Peter E. C. Dashwood <dashwood@enternet.co.nz> wrote:
>I was fascinated by Ken's post. It raises a number of issues.
>
…[26 more quoted lines elided]…
>indeed, .30c profit...)?

I did not know that a company's obligations to its employees were 
predicated upon profits; I believe that in most countries a company is 
obliged to act in a lawful manner... no more, no less.

>
>The Doc says their obligation is to do their utmost for the
>Shareholders.

Pardon me for my lack of precision; I stated this not as an expression of 
opinion but as an expression of common practise in the USA, where 
maximising shareholder return is considered a corporate duty.  (Oddly 
enough, in the state of Delaware - sometimes called 'The Corporate Fiefdom 
of DuPont' - a legal decision was handed down that stated an executive 
board which was enriching itsself at the cost of the shareholders was 
*not* guilty of any legal malfeasance.)

>
>(As a shareholder myself in various Companies, I have great sympathy
>for this point of view, and it would be a brave person indeed who
>would argue against it...<G>)

The argument appears to be against the functioning of the WIFFM gene... 
you know, that chunk of chromosome that cries out 'What's In It For Me?'

>
>But should this pursuit of profit be to the exclusion of all else?

Well, there *are* laws and such... ignore those at your own peril.

>
>Personally, I don't think so...
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>maximisation of profit MUST be done?

infinitely high price and for which there is an unending, infinitely large

>In article <b3638c46.0210230325.36565052@posting.google.com>,

This is an interesting development as BOA is one of my companies
clients and we do offer and have outsourcing contracts.  I'm not sure
of what we are doing for BOA right now but I know we are doing some
projects for them.  But what is even more astounding is that it is the
Charlotte group that is being impacted.  BOA has programming staffs
elsewhere.  The Charlotte group I believe is the former Nations Bank
group.  BOA bought Nations some time back.  I suspect this would have
happened sooner or later anyway.  Banks always start cutting
technology staff once they get everything converted over to one system
and learn where all the redundancy is at.  

As for the moral or ethical implications here, I believe it to be as
Doc has stated.  That the Bank management must do what is best for the
owners of the company, i.e., the shareholders.  Companies do things
for employees more in order to keep them thus reducing training and
recruiting costs and thus increasing profits.  In addition, long term
employees generally are more productive because they already know the
best way around a system.  Again this results in a cost benefit.  

While some "family" owned business may feel a moral or ethical
obligation to try and keep employees as long as they can at the
expense of profits, publicly owned businesses here in the USA are
required by various laws to think owners (shareholders) first.

On 23-Oct-2002, dashwood@enternet.co.nz (Peter E. C. Dashwood) wrote:

> But should this pursuit of profit be to the exclusion of all else?
>
> Personally, I don't think so.

Replace "profit" with "value".    Long term value to the stockholders includes
things other than current profits.


> I was surprised by this because you wouldn't think that shareholders
> would vote against their own interests. Nevertheless, on that
> occasion, they did.

Every choice we make is "against our own interests" to some degree, as all
choices have costs.  But when we make choices we are deciding which results net
out to be best for our own interests.

But we often make choices without thinking through everything.   For instance,
when we boycott Nike for building sweatshops in poor countries, we are often
telling them to shut down the sweatshops that have provided a welcome
alternative to slash and burn economy - and telling them to send their employees
out to destroy the jungles and starve again.    (They won't pay them our wages,
as we are more productive than they are).

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Bank of America is UN-AMERICAN

_(thread depth: 7)_

- **From:** riplin@Azonic.co.nz (Richard)
- **Date:** 2002-10-24T11:39:35-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<217e491a.0210241039.41068210@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<ap4omp$7mt$1@nntp2-cm.news.eni.net> <ap5155$l0e$1@panix1.panix.com> <b3638c46.0210230325.36565052@posting.google.com> <Wg-dnXGZGP5nMCugXTWcoA@giganews.com> <ap6d6o$hce$1@peabody.colorado.edu> <217e491a.0210231259.5ddb8ff2@posting.google.com> <ap8umh$66v$1@peabody.colorado.edu>`

```
"Howard Brazee" <howard.brazee@cusys.edu> wrote
> 
> > These type of statements also affect how suppliers and customers may
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> best for everybody.

You are rather confused, 'Insider trading' is entirely specific to the
one market for stocks and shares.  It does not apply in any way to the
actual 'marketplace' or to 'competition' (as implied by
supplier/customer).

In the case of the share market there is _no_ 'full knowledge' about
what they are buying, beacuse, sa you said, this is incompatible with
insider trading requirements.  If you have 'full knowledge' then you
are not allowed to trade.

In the actual marketplace you may have 'full knowledge' about what you
are buying but may have no knowledge about what others are buying, or
the price they are paying, nor what others are offering at what price.
You are rather naieve if you think that 'full disclosure' ever occurs,
or would benefit the discloser.
```

"JerryMouse" <nospam@bisusa.com> wrote in message
news:Wg-dnXGZGP5nMCugXTWcoA@giganews.com...
>
> No case has been made that the corporation must, as a matter of policy,
give
> a fig about the local community.

My recollection is that Bank of America started out as a California
institution called "Bank of Italy".  Presumably at some point the entirety
of its staff was in California, and I believe at one time their corporate
offices were in San Francisco though I'm not absolutely certain that it
wasn't Los Angeles.  In any event, their offices and thus their corporate
staff were once in an area that has among the highest costs of living in
this country, which in turn tends to lead to higher salary expectations on
the part of the staff.

Lo and behold, with the emphasis on, and increase in, interstate banking
over the past couple of decades, I now note tha the headquarters of the Bank
of America are in Charlotte, North Carolina.  Charlotte is a lovely city,
from all I have heard, but a quick look at www.homeseekers.com tells me I
can by a large and VERY nice home on a huge lot in a great neighborhood for
what a run-down bungalow in a crime-ridden area of Los Angeles would cost.
San Francisco (and Bay Area) real estate, and salaries, are even higher.  I
would be very surprised if the salaries offered in Charlotte were anywhere
near as high as those in either of these cities, job for job.

Thus, it appears to me that some time back the Powers That Be in BofA
decided to relocate their Information Technology programming functions from
one location (the West Coast) to another (Charlotte) to reduce costs, and
thereby increase profits for their shareholders.

Now it seems that the Powers That Be in BofA decided to relocate their
Information Technology programming functions from one location (Charlotte)
to another (India) to reduce costs, and thereby increase profits for their
shareholders.

The first is Sound Business Judgment, and the second is an outrage and an
affront to the community.

??????

    -Chuck Stevens

JerryMouse wrote:
> "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@enternet.co.nz>
> 
…[33 more quoted lines elided]…
> they made the right decision at the next stockholders' meeting.

This an idealized view of corporate governance, much like the board is 
supposed to be making sure the CEO is doing a good job. In real life 
they're generally buddies and poor performance gets rewarded anyway. 
It's very difficult to force someone out because it requires getting 
more board members to vote against the current management than current 
management already has a relationship with.

>>Some years ago I attended an AGM of the German Company BAYER (they of
>>aspirin fame...although many people would not realise that Bayer are
…[25 more quoted lines elided]…
> employing Ubangies.

>>reason to believe it wasn't.)
…[36 more quoted lines elided]…
> the stockholders decide.

Maximizing profits is, of course, the objective of a business. However, 
the current focus on maximizing profits and the rest be damned is a 
relatively recent phenomenon from the 80's, when the corporate gloves 
came off and greed was declared good. Prior to that companies were 
expected to be good corporate citizens and to give some thought to their 
employee's welfare. Loyalty to the company was generally rewarded by 
keeping one's job and when times got tough, people were let go starting 
with the fewest years of service, i.e., based on seniority.

My $0.02, anyway, YMMV

#### ↳ Re: Bank of America is UN-AMERICAN

- **From:** gary drummond <gdrumm@sbcglobal.net>

```
Ken Mullins wrote:
> 
> http://www.charlotte.com/mld/charlotte/business/industries/banking/4338944.h
…[36 more quoted lines elided]…
> "I call it being fired," one programmer said.

***WARNING-I'm on my soapbox again!***

Well, I've been gone from the group for awhile, but this does prompt a
few questions from me and I would guess a few others.

1. Has anyone wondered about al Quaida only having to go "next-door", to
cause problems which will cause our ecomomy to suffer? (Firewalls from
Israel, Cisco support from India, Legacy program support from India and
others in the area...)

2. Salaries NOT paid to American workers will mean money NOT spent in
America, which means which means less income in America, which means
MORE out-sourcing to foreign countries to save dollars, and even LESS
money deposited in American banks?

3. With most of our chips made in foreign countries, and so much of our
defense systems dependent on technology, expressed through the larger
and larger reliance on chips made in a foreign country, could we be
allowing ANYONE to destroy our ability to defend ourselves?

As far as COBOL goes (to keep this in the NG :-) all we have to do it
wait and charge the BAC and others 20-50 times our original salaries, to
recover after any of the above (assuming we are still alive...)

For all the conversions to C, C++, Java, and ???... just wait for the
companies to get the facts about none of them being able to handle
"real" dollars and cents. I experienced the problems at one website
where it took a C programmer a little over 3 weeks to modify the libs,
AFTER they bought the source code, to do decimal math correctly. (I only
stayed 2 months there because I knew they would find even more problems!
This sounds a lot like supporting local programs VS "the new STANDARD
[cheaper programmers]" programs!)

When I learned asm and fortran on my mainframe, I wrote a program to
compute my paycheck. We got extra for nights and weekends or both.
Fortran didn't round, so I wrote it in asm, which made me scale by 100
until I printed the results. Floating point in asm was just like
fortran. The good point is that my mainframe could handle anything up to
4,722,366,482,869,645,213,695 for integers, and scaling by 100 was no
problem at all for MY paycheck! I learned COBOL after that, which made
everything better. Using Java, C, C#, and whatever the M$/Unix gurus
said to use doesn't seem to save any money, it just gets harder to
support!

Oh well, everyone except the stockholders will be retired and have their
CASH before any of the above happens, so I guess the rest of us will
just have to pay for it, unless we can live long enough to fix all of
it!

I feel better now. (Again!)

Gary
```

#### ↳ Re: Bank of America is UN-AMERICAN

- **From:** poopiehead <member@dbforums.com>
- **Date:** 2002-10-30T13:12:49+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1990004.1035983569@dbforums.com>`
- **References:** `<ap4omp$7mt$1@nntp2-cm.news.eni.net>`

```

It is a dangerous notion to believe that either the host or non-host
nation will be bettered.  We have seen in the past with such great
legislative acts such as NAFTA that neither country betters itself.
First:  Local employment is lost and less spending is generated.  This
causes a sort of chain reaction.  Many of the former employees take
lower paying jobs to get by.  Which in turn allows them to spend much
less and negatively effects the rest of the ecomomy.  With a higher rate
of unemployment you tend to generate lower wages, since demand for
certain skills becomes a lot less.  This causes more wage drops which
continues this chain reaction.
I would say that many if not most large companies are adopting this
hazardous approach to business.  Some of the large compaines include
Microsoft (Having large portions of its programming done in India), Ford
(Having parts assembled and manufactured in foriegn soils), BMW (Opened
a plant in North Carolina after American wages fell below German wages),
Misys (English Company that contracts programmers in India and has

livelyhood.

industrial nations' businesses.  This forces labor money to come
straight back to the industrail nation.  Which means that the 3rd world
nation economy isn't being built up.  We are seeing this with NAFTA

### ScrollBar in Totem

- **From:** joey76 <member@dbforums.com>
- **Date:** 2002-10-23T08:25:19+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1961533.1035361519@dbforums.com>`

```

Hi!
I can manage a large amount of entry-field (a ministerial model) in a
Screen designed with Totem 6.1 (The new Acubench by acucorp).
My problem is this:the size of the screen its more great than the size
of the screen (at any acceptable resolution).
When the focus pass to an entry-field that isn't visible on the screen
the screen don't scroll automatically.But isn't possible manage the
scroll of the window by any cobol command or by any Windows Api.

There are a OCX that resolve my problem?

Someone can help me?
Please!!

thanks
joey
```

#### ↳ Re: ScrollBar in Totem

- **From:** "Grinder" <grinder@no.spam.maam.com>
- **Date:** 2002-10-23T22:45:04-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ap7qc202g43@enews2.newsguy.com>`
- **References:** `<1961533.1035361519@dbforums.com>`

```

"joey76" <member@dbforums.com> wrote in message
news:1961533.1035361519@dbforums.com...
>
> Hi!
> I can manage a large amount of entry-field (a ministerial
model) in a
> Screen designed with Totem 6.1 (The new Acubench by acucorp).
> My problem is this:the size of the screen its more great than
the size
> of the screen (at any acceptable resolution).
> When the focus pass to an entry-field that isn't visible on
the screen
> the screen don't scroll automatically.But isn't possible
manage the
> scroll of the window by any cobol command or by any Windows
Api.

I can't speak to the scrollbar or control implementations in
Totem, but if you must do this, the logic would be:

1)  When a control gets focus, determine if it is visible.

     You may need to inspect the scrollbar's value and use
that, with information about the client area of your window, to
calculate it's position relative to that client area.

2)  If it is not visible, determine the closest scrollbar
position that would make it visible -- and set that value.

It seems unlikely that anything native to COBOL will help here.
The Windows API could be used, I suppose, but any information
you need _should_ be exposed by the control's properties.
```

#### ↳ Re: ScrollBar in Totem

- **Date:** 2002-10-23T20:23:11-07:00

field to existing screen which is defined as length = 02.  While I do
the test, I found amazing thing is that actual field length more than

help me to find out what's the possible reason for that ? Or any
method for testing the actual reason for that ? Thanks adance for your
help. Thanks.

The BMS Mapset :
BRNOTE   DFHMDF POS=(20,60),LENGTH=02,ATTRB=(UNPROT,FSET),

               JUSTIFY=(RIGHT,ZERO),PICOUT='99'                       
 02384000

Off the top of my head you need to close the field.  Although the
program will only accept 2 bytes the screen has no skip after this
field and so allows the entry of more data.  Try something like

DFHMDF POS=(20,63),ATTRB=(ASKIP),LENGTH=01

#### ↳ Re: field length error for COBOL/CICS online program

- **From:** robert@jones0086.freeserve.co.uk (Robert Jones)
- **Date:** 2002-10-24T10:41:12-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<fcd09c56.0210240941.31760828@posting.google.com>`

```
Hello Calvin, 

Answers below your question:

calvin5867705@yahoo.com (link) wrote in message news:<5d879bfe.0210231923.77ba1333@posting.google.com>...
> Hi,
> 
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
>  02384000

It been a while since I last used CICS, but I think what you need to
follow your new field is a stopper byte, which can be defined as
follows:

           DFHMDF POS=(20,62),LENGTH=1,ATTRB=(ASKIP,NORM),LENGTH=01

You will probably see similar examples of stopper bytes in your
pre-existing mapset, one after each real field.

Hope this Helps, Robert
```

#### ↳ Re: Net Express

- **From:** "Gazaloo" <gaz@a.loo>
- **Date:** 2002-10-27T00:02:19+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<e2Gu9.112283$md1.23356@sccrnsc03>`
- **References:** `<1970864.1035548300@dbforums.com>`

```
Alain, current release of NX is V3.1 Service Pack 1 -- V4.0 is under
development and should appear in the 1st half of 2003.

The CGI app that you develop under NX can be moved with no source changes to
Server Express on AIX. Infact you can use NX to publish your application to
Server Express.

I've also attached a simple COBOL CGI program to this response. You may find
it useful.

--Gazaloo.

A nice/slick alternative to using external-forms to output a page is to
simply embed the HTML into your program. in this case the 01 output-page
item is not needed and instead of the 'display output-page', you have:

exec html
    copy "output.htm"
end exec

You can also code HTML directly; you don't have to use copybooks. A pretty
simple, COBOL/SQL-like implementation.

==>start of cobolcgi source
identification division.

working-storage section.
01 input-page is external-form.
   03  name-field pic x(30) identified by "Name".
   03  phone-no   pic x(30) identified by "Phone".
   03  email      pic x(30) identified by "Email".

01 output-page is external-form identified by "output".
   03  name-field pic x(30) identified by "Name".
   03  phone-no   pic x(30) identified by "Phone".
   03  email      pic x(30) identified by "Email".

procedure division.

    accept input-page
    move corresponding input-page to output-page
    display output-page
    .
==>end of cobolcgi source

==>start of input.htm
<HTML>
<HEAD>
<TITLE>Sample Form for Net Express</TITLE>
</HEAD>
<BODY>

<P>COBOL Input Form

<FORM METHOD="POST" ACTION="/cgi-bin/cobolcgi.exe"></P>
<PRE>
Name     <INPUT TYPE="TEXT" NAME="Name" VALUE="" MAXLENGTH="30" >
Email id <INPUT TYPE="TEXT "NAME="Email" VALUE="" MAXLENGTH="30" >
Phone    <INPUT NAME="Phone" VALUE="" MAXLENGTH="12">
<INPUT TYPE="SUBMIT" VALUE="Send Form"><INPUT TYPE="RESET">
</PRE>
</FORM>

</BODY>
</HTML>
==>end of input.htm

==>start of output.htm
<HTML>

<P>*** SAMPLE OUTPUT FORM ***</P>
<P>Dear :name-field</P>
<P>blah blah blah</P>

</HTML>
==>end of output.htm
```

## Thread: call-convention — 2 msgs

### call-convention

- **From:** "dsoans" <dsoans@rogers.com>

```
I have code that was written in Micro Focus COBOL and is using the
CALL-CONVENTION statement as:
CALL-CONVENTION 2 IS ODBCAPI

I need to now compile with CA-Realia II and have problems with this line. I
get the error:
81 ( 10) 0508 E EBCDIC or STANDARD-N expected; found '2'

81 ( 10) 0112 E Unrecognizable word or literal 'IS'

81 ( 10) 0508 E EBCDIC or STANDARD-N expected; found '.'



Is the CALL-CONVENTION statement specific to Micro Focus COBOL or is it part
of the general COBOL standard? If anyone has any ideas on how I can recode
this please share them with me.

Thank you.

Dennis

```
I use Realia Workbench but do not use the CALL-CONVENTION. It seems that the
programmer was trying to access a data file via ODBC. I do use ODBC and
Realia all the time and it is done via a pre-compiler that you set up via
the Workbench. I hope this helps.

## Thread: Question about ISPF/PDF editor usage for COPY/PASTE within two session — 11 msgs

_Topics: [`Language features and syntax`](topics.md#syntax) · [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe)_

### Question about ISPF/PDF editor usage for COPY/PASTE within two session

- **From:** calvin5867705@yahoo.com (link)
- **Date:** 2002-10-26T21:43:38-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<5d879bfe.0210262043.29ba86b7@posting.google.com>`

```
How can I share the information between two ISPF/PDF sessions ?

For exmaple, If I have one PDF session open right now. I put C Command
for one lines copying from.  Then I open the second session (press F2
key )and the corresponding file, and put A Command. When i press enter
key. I get the message "COPY/MOVE PENDING". which means the copy is
not successful.

Can anyone tell me what is the problem for that ? Or I need any
profile setting ???

Thanks a lot for your answer.

(It runs perfect within one seesion editor.)
```

#### ↳ Re: Question about ISPF/PDF editor usage for COPY/PASTE within two session

- **From:** gregjohnson@comcast.net
- **Date:** 2002-10-27T01:14:31-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<rv0nru8iptvef16er4hn8l71437fqukoao@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<5d879bfe.0210262043.29ba86b7@posting.google.com>`

```
You have to use the CUT and PASTE commands on the command line when
you have muliple sessions open.



On 26 Oct 2002 21:43:38 -0700, calvin5867705@yahoo.com (link) wrote:

>How can I share the information between two ISPF/PDF sessions ?
>

#### ↳ Re: Question about ISPF/PDF editor usage for COPY/PASTE within two session

- **From:** "Hugh Candlin" <no@spam.com>
- **Date:** 2002-10-27T07:12:54+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<WlMu9.8094$VJ5.459303@bgtnsc05-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`
- **References:** `<5d879bfe.0210262043.29ba86b7@posting.google.com>`

```

link <calvin5867705@yahoo.com> wrote in message news:5d879bfe.0210262043.29ba86b7@posting.google.com...
> How can I share the information between two ISPF/PDF sessions ?
>
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
> (It runs perfect within one seesion editor.)

I usually require this capability when transferring blocks of code
from one PDS member to another.

I have 3 techniques which I find useful, depending on the situation.

1  I copy PDS member #1 in its entirety to the end of PDS member #2.
    Then I clean up PDS member #2.  I block delete the lines I don't want.
    When I find some old member #1 code that I want to keep, I block move it
     to where it needs to be.

2  I open both PDS members in the same PDS, even if I have to move
    one of them in temporarily from another PDS.  When I find some code
    that I want to keep, I CC the block and enter CRE TT on the command line
    and hit <Enter>.  That creates a new PDS member called TT containing
    the code I want to transfer.  Then I click over to my other session,
    enter A at my insert point, and type MOVE TT on the command line.
    Once I've got this going, and have a number of such moves, I simply
    use PF12 to restore the commands so that I don't have to keep typing them.

3  I use straight cut-and-paste or copy-and-paste.  For example, if I have 9 lines
    to move or copy, I highlight it and cut it (deleting the blank lines created),
    or copy it, find my insert point, type I9 to create the necessary blank lines,
    and then paste.

The only difficult part is to stay focused on the task when it gets repetitive.
```

```
On 26 Oct 2002 21:43:38 -0700 calvin5867705@yahoo.com (link) wrote:

:>How can I share the information between two ISPF/PDF sessions ?

:>For exmaple, If I have one PDF session open right now. I put C Command
:>for one lines copying from.  Then I open the second session (press F2
:>key )and the corresponding file, and put A Command. When i press enter
:>key. I get the message "COPY/MOVE PENDING". which means the copy is
:>not successful.

:>Can anyone tell me what is the problem for that ? Or I need any
:>profile setting ???

You would have to program it.

ISPF/PDF Edit does not have a copy from screen to screen function.

You can use the CUT and PASTE macros to do the trick, but this will involve
first completing the CUT function on the source screen, SWAPping, and issuing
the PASTE function.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Question about ISPF/PDF editor usage for COPY/PASTE within two session

- **From:** jacksleight@hotmail.com (Jack Sleight)
- **Date:** 2002-10-27T21:56:36-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8a2d426e.0210272156.631af2d8@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<5d879bfe.0210262043.29ba86b7@posting.google.com> <pv9nruof2ivho0t6hks5rmr3ub08u7qf7u@4ax.com>`

```
Some other thoughts that may be useful:

You can cut multiple times before pasting and the aggregate lines cut
will appear in the pasted PDS member in the same order that they were
cut.

BTW, if you cut and don't paste, and cut again later in the same ISPF
session, both cuts will appear in the pasted PDS member.

As I recall, you can avoid the above situation by using a name in the
cut command, i.e.: cut cutnbr1. If you cut again, use another name.
When you paste, though, you must use the appropriate name to recall
the desired data.

Jack

Binyamin Dissen <postingid@dissensoftware.com> wrote in message news:<pv9nruof2ivho0t6hks5rmr3ub08u7qf7u@4ax.com>...

> the PASTE function.

by setting an optional parameter.

Otherwise, a second cut or copy without an intervening paste
will overlay and negate the first cut or copy.

However, I don't remember if it is a Windows option
(don't think so), an ExtraPC! option, or (probably) an ISPF option.

## Thread: "Now is the time for all "Good COBOLer's ..." — 6 msgs

### "Now is the time for all "Good COBOLer's ..."

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-10-27T13:56:26-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<aphgde$ggj$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
Believe it or not (and consider it "good or bad" as you will <G>),

  *** NOW ***

is the time for anyone interested in providing input into the *next* COBOL
Standard (the one after the recently approved 2002 Standard) to provide
their input (including both ideas and PRIORITIES) to the COBOL
Standardization committees.

For a current list of items that have been suggested (some of which have
been discussed - others which have not), you can see the J4 document
"Candidate features for a future revision" at:

    http://www.cobolportal.com/j4/files/02-0222.doc

Just because an item is listed there, please do NOT assume that it either
will be or won't be on the "work plan" for the next revision.  If you have
input on this list (including items to ADD, Delete, or that you want to
express an opinion on its priority), you can do one of two things (and I
recommend the first)

FYI - before "pursuing" this, you probably will want to review the
"Substantive Change" section of the 2002 Standard to see if the feature that
you are interested in, has already been "included" - but isn't (yet)
available from your COBOL Vendor-of-choice.

1) Send a note to the J4 chair at:

 Don.Schricker <at > microfocus.com

giving as MUCH detail as possible on what you want and why you want it (and
where you rank its priority compared to other things - including length of
time until next Standard, e.g.

  "I want you to add feature XYZ - because we are forced to use non-COBOL
features to do the following 'business task' ... and I want this feature
more than most/some/many of the other items currently listed in 02-0222.
Please do <not> add this feature if it will take more than (2? 3? 5?) years
to process the next COBOL Standard."

2) If you are involved in COBOL "work" in some country outside the US, then
you can send this same information to your national Standards body.  For a
list of how to contact such groups, see:


http://www.iso.org/iso/en/aboutiso/isomembers/MemberList.MemberSummary?MEMBE
RCODE=10

(Going thru your own national Standards body *might* give it higher priority
than going thru J4 - which people from ANY country can submit ideas to.
However, it also may DELAY the processing - as the international group will
PROBABLY end up referring it back to J4.)

P.S. If there is an idea listed in the "02-0222" document listed above that
you want more information on.  You can probably get this from the J4 chair.
Some of them already have detailed "suggestion" papers, some have only
sketchy suggestions, and some only have a sentence or two in some other
document.
```

## Thread: Comprehensive listing of errors — 4 msgs

### Comprehensive listing of errors

- **From:** "Dawn Minnis" <dawn_minnis@thefreeinternet.co.uk>
- **Date:** 2002-10-27T22:17:42+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<aphom5$55e$1@helle.btinternet.com>`

```
does anybody know where i can find a really good (and by that I mean fully
explained) list of complie and runtime errors for COBOL.  My list has
basically 5-6 word answers that dont really explain anything.

Any Ideas

Dawn
```

#### ↳ Re: Comprehensive listing of errors

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-10-27T16:55:12-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<aphqsk$ntn$1@slb3.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<aphom5$55e$1@helle.btinternet.com>`

```
Tell us what compiler (vendor, release, and operating system) you are
interested in.

IBM's mainframe compiler (for example) will give you a complete list of
compile-time messages - if you simply compile a program with

  IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
  PROGRAM-ID.  ERRMSG.

    ***

Other vendors provide "message" manuals - while others say that there
messages are "self-documenting".
```

#### ↳ Re: Comprehensive listing of errors

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2002-10-27T23:29:20+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<kF_u9.1393$mN6.418300@newssrv26.news.prodigy.com>`
- **References:** `<aphom5$55e$1@helle.btinternet.com>`

```
"Dawn Minnis" <dawn_minnis@thefreeinternet.co.uk> wrote in message
news:aphom5$55e$1@helle.btinternet.com...
> does anybody know where i can find a really good (and by that I mean fully
> explained) list of complie and runtime errors for COBOL.  My list has
> basically 5-6 word answers that dont really explain anything.

All compile and run-time error codes are defined by the compiler publisher.
No such thing as a common set of error codes. If your compiler provides 5-6
words, that's what you get.

About the only COBOL 'code values' which are [semi]-standardized are FILE
STATUS values.

MCM
```

---

concatenation!).


Bj�rn

news:VA.00000287.053afe3b@ieee.org...

>
> > The should be able to read files with fixed variable
> > record sizes, ie. every time the program is executed the input is a
fixed

```

#### ↳ Re: Universal record size

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2002-10-29T12:14:16+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<sYuv9.2232$mN6.645976@newssrv26.news.prodigy.com>`
- **References:** `<3dbd8c6b$0$28830$edfadb0f@dspool01.news.tele.dk> <VA.00000287.053afe3b@ieee.org> <3dbe1790$0$97659$edfadb0f@dspool01.news.tele.dk>`

```
ENVIRONMENT DIVISION

            SELECT FIXED-LENGTH-VARIABLE-FILE
             ORGANIZATION SEQUENTIAL
             ACCESS SEQUENTIAL
            ASSIGN TO  whatever

FILE SECTION.
FD FIXED-LENGTH-VARIABLE-FILE
  RECORD IS VARYING IN SIZE FROM n1 TO n2 CHARACTERS
     DEPENDING ON FLV-LENGTH
01 DATA         PIC X(N2).

WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
01 FLV-LENGTH  PIC 9(04) USAGE COMP.

(Syntax might be slightly off but it's close).

FLV-LENGTH will contain record length after each successful READ. (And must
be set to correct value before doing any WRITE).
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Universal record size

- **From:** "Charles Hottel" <chottel@cpcug.org>
- **Date:** 2002-10-30T00:25:01+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<01c27faa$c62cfc40$4d95f243@chottel>`
- **References:** `<3dbd8c6b$0$28830$edfadb0f@dspool01.news.tele.dk> <VA.00000287.053afe3b@ieee.org> <3dbe1790$0$97659$edfadb0f@dspool01.news.tele.dk> <sYuv9.2232$mN6.645976@newssrv26.news.prodigy.com>`

```
If you understand Cobol pointers you could use them to point to the DCB for
the file.  The layout/map/DSECT for the DCB can be found in the assembler
macro  DCBD DSORG=PS.  You want the displacement to the DCBLRECL field. You
can use this record length to set FLV-LENGHT in Mike's sample code.  Here
is a sample program that use pointers. Look for the part that addresses the
DCB:

//JOBNAME JOB (ACCT,'ROOM-NBR'),'HOTTEL COBPTR',MSGCLASS=S,CLASS=K         
    
//PROCLIB JCLLIB ORDER=USERID.DVL.PROC                                     
    
//        SET TITLE1='XXX.COB00010'                                        
    
//OUTPUT INCLUDE MEMBER=DESTCH                                             
    
//*-------------------------------------------------------------------*    
    
//*        COBOL II COMPILE                                           *    
    
//*-------------------------------------------------------------------*    
    
//STEP01   EXEC  COB3CLG,LIBRARY='DVL.SOURCE.LIBMAST',PROG=IEFBR14,        
    
//    LOPT='AMODE=31,RMODE=ANY'                                            
    
//COMP.SYSIN DD  *                                                         
    
       ID DIVISION.                                                        
    
       PROGRAM-ID.   COBPTR.                                               
    
       AUTHOR.       CHARLIE HOTTEL.                                       
    
       DATE-WRITTEN. 08/22/01.                                             
    
       DATE-COMPILED.                                                      
    
      *---------------------------------------------------------------*    
    
      *    VS COBOL II POINTER FEATURE EXAMPLE                        *    
    
      *    USING MVS CONTROL BLOCKS                                   *    
    
      *---------------------------------------------------------------*    
    
      *    BASED ON ARTICLE: "THE POINTER FEATURE OF VS COBOL II" BY  *    
    
      *    ANNE PETICOLAS IN ENTERPRISE SYSTEMS JOURNAL, MARCH 1991.  *    
    
      *---------------------------------------------------------------*    
    
       ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.                                               
    
       INPUT-OUTPUT SECTION.                                               
    
       FILE-CONTROL.                                                       
    
           SELECT TEST-FILE ASSIGN TO DD1.                                 
    
       DATA DIVISION.                                                      
    
       FILE SECTION.                                                       
    
       FD  TEST-FILE                                                       
    
           LABEL RECORDS STANDARD                                          
    
           RECORDING MODE IS F                                             
    
           BLOCK CONTAINS 0 RECORDS                                        
    
           DATA RECORD IS TEST-REC.                                        
    
       01  TEST-REC PIC X(80).                                             
    
      /                                                                    
    
       WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.                                            
    
                                                                           
    
TEST***01  WS-TEST                            PIC S9(9) COMP VALUE ZERO.   
    
       01  WS-WORK                             PIC S9(9) COMP.             
    
       01  WS-RIGHT-HEX-DIGIT                  PIC S9(4) COMP.             
    
       01  WS-LEN                              PIC S9(4) COMP.             
    
       01  WS-LENGTH REDEFINES WS-LEN          PIC X(02).                  
    
       01  WS-FLAG                             PIC S9(4) COMP.             
    
       01  WS-FLAG1 REDEFINES WS-FLAG          PIC X(02).                  
    
                                                                           
    
       01  WS-TCB-ADDRESS-POINTER.                                         
    
           05  WS-TCB-ADDR-POINTER             USAGE IS POINTER.           
    
                                                                           
    
       01  WS-TIOT-SEG-POINT.                                              
    
           05  WS-TIOT-SEG-POINTER             USAGE IS POINTER.

                                               PIC S9(9) COMP.             
    
                                                                           
    
       01  WS-JFCB-POINT.                                                  
    
           05  WS-JFCB-POINTER                 USAGE IS POINTER.           
    
           05  WS-JFCB-PTR REDEFINES WS-JFCB-POINTER

           05  WS-JFCB-POINT-RED REDEFINES  WS-JFCB-PTR.                   
    
               07  FILLER                      PIC X.                      
    
               07  WS-JFCB-LOW-3               PIC X(3).

           05  WS-POINTER                      USAGE IS POINTER.

                                               PIC S9(9) COMP.

               07  FILLER                      PIC X.                      
    
               07  WS-LOW-3                    PIC X(3).

      /                                                                    
    
      *---------------------------------------------------------------*    
    
      * PUT THE STATEMENTS BELOW IN AN ASSEMBLER PROGRAM TO LOCATE    *
